  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c6120ce8-21d4-4a27-9284-79652428dd88'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4675346142428207634">The graphic novel debut from rising star Noelle Stevenson, based on her beloved and critically acclaimed web comic, which Slate awarded its Cartoonist Studio Prize, calling it "a deadpan epic."<br/><br/>Nemeses! Dragons! Science! Symbolism! All these and more await in this brilliantly subversive, sharply irreverent epic from Noelle Stevenson. Featuring an exclusive epilogue not seen</span>
  <span id="freeText4675346142428207634" style="display:none">The graphic novel debut from rising star Noelle Stevenson, based on her beloved and critically acclaimed web comic, which Slate awarded its Cartoonist Studio Prize, calling it "a deadpan epic."<br /><br />Nemeses! Dragons! Science! Symbolism! All these and more await in this brilliantly subversive, sharply irreverent epic from Noelle Stevenson. Featuring an exclusive epilogue not seen in the web comic, along with bonus conceptual sketches and revised pages throughout, this gorgeous full-color graphic novel is perfect for the legions of fans of the web comic and is sure to win Noelle many new ones.<br /><br />Nimona is an impulsive young shapeshifter with a knack for villainy. Lord Ballister Blackheart is a villain with a vendetta. As sidekick and supervillain, Nimona and Lord Blackheart are about to wreak some serious havoc. Their mission: prove to the kingdom that Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin and his buddies at the Institution of Law Enforcement and Heroics aren't the heroes everyone thinks they are.<br /><br />But as small acts of mischief escalate into a vicious battle, Lord Blackheart realizes that Nimona's powers are as murky and mysterious as her past. And her unpredictable wild side might be more dangerous than he is willing to admit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4675346142428207634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='questionText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/523372-are-ballister-and-ambrosius-former-lovers"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Are Ballister and Ambrosius former lovers who end up back in a romantic relationship in the epilogue, or is this "queerbaiting", i.e. heavy-handed hints at queer romance that are characterized as friendship to appease potentially homophobic readers? I was sure the characters would speak their feelings for each other by book's end and was surprised to see the last panel of the epilogue paint them as *FRIENDS!* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37877332-lara-willard"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1460927161i/37877332._UX100_CR0,8,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37877332-lara-willard">Lara Willard</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Queer is canon. Stevenson has plenty of artwork corroborating the relationship and in an interview with the A.V. Club says:<br /><br />"There was a situation wher<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Queer is canon. Stevenson has plenty of artwork corroborating the relationship and in an interview with the A.V. Club says:<br /><br />"There was a situation where the two lead knights in Nimona, as I was working on it, came to the realization that not only were they former best friends, but they had been romantically involved in the past. And I didn’t really know because I figured that out so late in the game how to incorporate that in to make it feel more natural." <br /><br />Her regretting the ambiguity in Nimona is why Lumberjanes is more explicit.<br /><br />Edit: Thalia's answer provided a great link (check it out!) with a similar quote from Stevenson:<br />"Ballister and Ambrosius are, canonically, former secret(-ish) boyfriends, but I must admit it wasn’t my intention from the beginning. It’s one of the things I’d change if I could do it all again - I’d make it clear, in the text, from the start. Both the Director and Goldenloin make reference towards it near the end, but I do feel convicted about the fact that none of the characters ever addressed it outright, especially since it’s a topic that’s very important to me, and moving forward I won’t make the same mistakes." <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_853').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14218739374533606793"><br/><i>
  <i>
    <b>‘‘I can’t have a kid following me around all day.’’<br/><br/>‘‘I’m not a kid. I’M A SHARK.’’</b>
  </i>
</i><br/><br/>Pouahaha. What a story! What witty dialogs! Filled with humour, adventure, magic and friendship, it will certainly charm and entertain the hell out of you. This title used to be a DNF of mine, before I decided to give it a second shot. Glad I did! What made me stop reading it the first time around was the graphics, because this is a style that never appealed to me, but truth is, it just grows on you, as</span>
  <span id="freeText14218739374533606793" style="display:none"><br><i>
  <i>
    <b>‘‘I can’t have a kid following me around all day.’’<br><br>‘‘I’m not a kid. I’M A SHARK.’’</b>
  </i>
</i><br><br>Pouahaha. What a story! What witty dialogs! Filled with humour, adventure, magic and friendship, it will certainly charm and entertain the hell out of you. This title used to be a DNF of mine, before I decided to give it a second shot. Glad I did! What made me stop reading it the first time around was the graphics, because this is a style that never appealed to me, but truth is, it just grows on you, as do the characters and every other element.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437599668i/15601214.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nimona, huge bear hugs to you. Ballister, you’ve got my admiration. Goldenloin, <u>I want your hair</u>. Noelle Stevenson, I wish you’d write a sequel or an happy-ever-after epilogue. I want to see Ballister &amp; Goldenloin kiss. <br><br><b>I loved it.</b><br></span>

<div id="review_1305195956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305195956" />
    <a title="Sean Gibson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson"><img alt="Sean Gibson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416866667p2/20955173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1305195956?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Gibson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Gibson" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson">Sean Gibson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38898402-nimona">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1305195956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5411001834984268691">4.8 Stars<br/><br/>Warning: Spoilers and mawkish sentiment ahead, and very few jokes (though that will be a relief to most of you). <br/><br/>At first blush, Nimona is the tale of a precocious but powerful girl’s quest to apprentice herself to the villainous Lord Ballister Blackheart as he fights the forces of good and justice, led by the spectacularly appellated (yes, I just verbed “appellation”...deal with it) Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin. As our tale begins, we learn that Nimona is a shapeshifter and can take the fo</span>
  <span id="freeText5411001834984268691" style="display:none">4.8 Stars<br /><br />Warning: Spoilers and mawkish sentiment ahead, and very few jokes (though that will be a relief to most of you). <br /><br />At first blush, Nimona is the tale of a precocious but powerful girl’s quest to apprentice herself to the villainous Lord Ballister Blackheart as he fights the forces of good and justice, led by the spectacularly appellated (yes, I just verbed “appellation”...deal with it) Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin. As our tale begins, we learn that Nimona is a shapeshifter and can take the form of any living creature, which makes her a formidable foe indeed, given that she gains the strength, mass, size, and requisite abilities of said creatures, and given that she lives in a world where dragons exist. <br /><br />The initial chapters read like a throwback to the Sunday funnies—discrete, episodic sequences complete with droll punchlines. “Charming,” I thought, settling in for a book-length collection of such strips.<br /><br />Only not so much. <br /><br />The book quickly morphs into something more complex, something deeper, something more melancholy—even as it is laugh-out-loud funny at times. Blackheart is a villain who won’t kill…and is he even a villain? Goldenloin is a hero with a dark secret representing an institute whose goals may be far more nefarious than anything Blackheart might ever dream up. And Nimona…Nimona is, by turns, a sarcastic girl, a lonely orphan, and a vicious killing machine. <br /><br />It’s impossible not to get instantly sucked into the world Stevenson creates, one where rules and logic are, to quote the great Peter Venkman, more of a guideline than a rule—knights with swords communicate via advanced video technology, and brilliant scientists and technologists discuss the merits and properties of magic. In other words, anything goes, so long as it fits the story. Stevenson’s art perfectly suits the world, and she creates fully realized and rendered characters with both words and pictures. <br /><br />There are some issues—for example, we want our wee Nimona to be a sympathetic character, but she IS a killer, plain and simple, and that doesn’t reconcile with how Blackheart in particular feels about her and treats her. But, that notwithstanding, I’m going to go full on fanboy here.<br /><br />This book is EXACTLY what non-spandex-clad-hero graphic novels should be: heartfelt, personal, and passionately executed. It’s the perfect fusion of art and story, of pathos and humor, of grace and glee. The relationship between estranged lovers Blackheart and Goldenloin is beautiful—it’s an eloquent, poignant no-statement statement, a romance between two men that requires no soapbox commentary because it’s not about social activism, but rather just the timeless tale of two people who love each other (albeit one in which one lover severed the other one’s arm and took years to apologize, but that’s neither here nor there). <br /><br />As a reader, I’m thankful that new media allows for so many ways for stories like this to be told and distributed, and for talented storytellers like Stevenson to find an audience.<br /><br />Okay, okay—enough with the sentimentality. I promise to return to inappropriate scatological humor in my next review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5411001834984268691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1550596496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1550596496" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1550596496?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062278234" href="/book/show/23131088-nimona">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1550596496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8497241848971461392"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398544796i/9432644._SX540_.jpg' width='440' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br/><br/>I’ve been meaning to read this graphic novel for a few months now and I’m really happy that I finally did.<br/>It had me hooked right from the beginning and wouldn’t let go till the end. I loved it!<br/><br/>This story follows Nimona, a shapeshifter, and Ballister Blackheart, a villain with a vendetta.<br/>They are partnering up as sidekick and supervillain, and are about to wreak some serious havoc. <br/>Their main mission: prove to the kingdom that Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin and his buddi</span>
  <span id="freeText8497241848971461392" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398544796i/9432644._SX540_.jpg" width="440" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br>I’ve been meaning to read this graphic novel for a few months now and I’m really happy that I finally did.<br>It had me hooked right from the beginning and wouldn’t let go till the end. I loved it!<br><br>This story follows Nimona, a shapeshifter, and Ballister Blackheart, a villain with a vendetta.<br>They are partnering up as sidekick and supervillain, and are about to wreak some serious havoc. <br>Their main mission: prove to the kingdom that Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin and his buddies at the Institution of Law Enforcement and Heroics aren't the heroes everyone thinks they are.<br><br>Reading <b>Nimona</b> was such an exhilarating journey. I felt as if I was right there with Ballister Blackheart and Nimona on their missions. They work so well together and their dialogue left me with the biggest smile on my face.<br><br><i>“What do you mean, there are rules? Why would you follow the rules? Isn’t that the whole point of being a villain, that you don’t follow the rules?”</i><br><br>I loved Nimona as a character, her enthusiasm, relatable humor, and her story really added depth to the plot. <br>She is as unique as the storyline.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457204661i/18333603._SY540_.jpg" width="540" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>I also enjoyed Ballister and Goldenloin, even though they definitely had a complicated journey at the beginning, I really liked them together.<br>They reminded me a bit of Baz and Simon from<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1555750401" rel="nofollow noopener"> Carry On</a> — I love them with all my heart.<br><br>Oh, and Doctor Blitzmeyer was a very pleasant surprise. I enjoyed reading about her and I would have loved it if Noelle Stevenson had added her journey to uncover the Anomalous Energy Enhancer.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457204661i/18333605._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>That ending left me in tears, I couldn’t believe it when Nimona didn’t get a happy ending. I was incredibly sad about it, that was such an emotional part of the story. I was just listening to sad music with tears in my eyes.<br><br><i>“Despite this tragedy, we remain united. We will stay strong, and we will rebuild.”</i> <br>But I kept thinking (until the very last page) ‘what about Nimona? She was left all alone at the end.’ <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457204661i/18333606._SY540_.jpg" width="540" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I was so thankful for the epilogue. I really thought for a second there that Noelle Stevenson would leave it on a cliffhanger.<br><br><br>So I’ve heard great things about this graphic novel, but the one that really got my attention was Rainbow Rowell’s blurb on the cover: <i>
  <b>“Full of humor and heart”</b>
</i>. I couldn’t agree more with her, she summed it perfectly up in just those 5 words.<br><b>Nimona</b> was an adventurous, heart-gripping, and humorous story — with amazing artwork. I love it!<br>Definitely a book that lived up to the hype.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457204661i/18333602._SX540_.png" width="540" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>Nimona</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0062278223/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0062278223&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=9c8c78ebbcf708e4647640bd463e0023" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482941769i/21564366.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482941769i/21564367.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1391620226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12186510802952032153">Lord Ballister Blackheart is a dastardly villain. Well, not really. He could be with the right little push.<br/>Enter Nimona!<br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442540269i/16249418._SX540_.jpg' alt='Chicago commercial photographers' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Nimona shows up one day and announces that she is now his side kick. She has some kick ass powers of shape-shifting. She can turn into any living thing. Even other human forms. The only form she can't take is something inanimate. <br/><br/>Nimona is primed to help Blackheart be the best super villain ever. If he would let her. She is ready to kill some people including the king. Hey,</span>
  <span id="freeText12186510802952032153" style="display:none">Lord Ballister Blackheart is a dastardly villain. Well, not really. He could be with the right little push.<br>Enter Nimona!<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442540269i/16249418._SX540_.jpg" alt="Chicago commercial photographers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nimona shows up one day and announces that she is now his side kick. She has some kick ass powers of shape-shifting. She can turn into any living thing. Even other human forms. The only form she can't take is something inanimate. <br><br>Nimona is primed to help Blackheart be the best super villain ever. If he would let her. She is ready to kill some people including the king. Hey, that's how kingdom's are taken over right?<br><br>Blackheart's main nemesis is his old friend Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin and his buddies at the Institution of Law Enforcement. Sir Ambrosius turned against Blackheart years ago and cost Blackheart his arm. (He now has a prosthetic) <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442540269i/16249419._SX540_.png" alt="Chicago commercial photographers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442540269i/16249420._SX540_.jpg" alt="Chicago commercial photographers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Even if he won't let our heroine express her little bloodthirsty heart to the full extent the duo manages to uncover secrets that the Institute wants kept under wraps.<br><br>With just small amounts of destruction in their wake....<br> <a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442540269i/16249421.jpg" alt="Chicago commercial photographers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book is great fun. I liked Nimona even though she is even more bloodthirsty than I am. Blackheart does well as the somewhat wussy villain and now I'm a convert to even this style of art. It took a few minutes to grow on me but in the end it did and the images fit the story.<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442540269i/16249422.jpg" alt="Chicago commercial photographers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283034987?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Carmen</a> is one of my favorite reviewers on Goodreads. She posts thought provoking and interesting reviews. Be sure and check her out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12186510802952032153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1438302636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1438302636" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590018789p2/10067920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1438302636?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062278234" href="/book/show/23131088-nimona">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438302636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9374101653077906627">I originally didn't plan on reading <em>Nimona</em>. I did not know about its history as a webcomic before sitting down to read it, and didn't know what to expect beyond the hype. But when I got it in a subscription box, I thought I'd give it a go. Ultimately, as per usual, the hype did the story a disservice.<br/><br/>I was actually surprised by how "meh" I felt about this story. First of all, I don't care for Noelle Stevenson's art style. Although I don't judge a graphic novel completely on its art style, it doe</span>
  <span id="freeText9374101653077906627" style="display:none">I originally didn't plan on reading <em>Nimona</em>. I did not know about its history as a webcomic before sitting down to read it, and didn't know what to expect beyond the hype. But when I got it in a subscription box, I thought I'd give it a go. Ultimately, as per usual, the hype did the story a disservice.<br /><br />I was actually surprised by how "meh" I felt about this story. First of all, I don't care for Noelle Stevenson's art style. Although I don't judge a graphic novel completely on its art style, it does have a slight impact on my enjoyment. Secondly, I found the characters to be mostly flat. Judging from the title, I thought this story was going to be about Nimona first and foremost, so I expected to feel some level of attachment to her. This story ended up focusing more on Ballister Blackheart, which in and of itself was my preference. I enjoy him as a character the most. But that also left Nimona to feel very one note. Also, I found the plot to be fairly predictable in a lot of ways.<br /><br />Lastly, I found myself annoyed with how Blackheart and Goldenloin weren't depicted in a way that blatantly showed they were gay. While, yes, it is obvious to most people, I have seen plenty of people say they are just "best friends." Fans of the webcomic may not have picked up on this, as I know that Noelle has since come out and said she is regretful for not making it blatant and does frequently show fanart or even her own art of them looking couple-y on her blog. Their romance (and friendship) was the heart of the story, and I felt it didn't quite achieve what it could because it held back.<br /><br />Overall, I found <em>Nimona</em> to be a cute story, but it did not live up to the overwhelming amount of hype and I've found it to be forgettable since I've read it. I'm more likely to recommend other graphic novels, even to new graphic novel readers.<a href="http://thoughtsontomes.com/2016/07/15/nimona-noelle-stevenson-review/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on Thoughts on Tomes</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9374101653077906627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1896713646" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896713646" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896713646?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062278234" href="/book/show/23131088-nimona">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896713646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1355636176394014542">I want to say, hands down, this book is amazing! Full of adventure, humor, awesome characters, giggle-inducing names, and plot twists -- “Nimona” is a beautiful mash-up of science fiction and fantasy. The story may follow the "villains”, but you will surely be rooting for them more and more with each turn of the page.<br/><br/>This is a fun, quick read with a lot of heart: featuring a villain who likes to play by the rules; his spunky sidekick who, well… doesn't; their "good-guy" arch-nemesis; and an orga</span>
  <span id="freeText1355636176394014542" style="display:none">I want to say, hands down, this book is amazing! Full of adventure, humor, awesome characters, giggle-inducing names, and plot twists -- “Nimona” is a beautiful mash-up of science fiction and fantasy. The story may follow the "villains”, but you will surely be rooting for them more and more with each turn of the page.<br /><br />This is a fun, quick read with a lot of heart: featuring a villain who likes to play by the rules; his spunky sidekick who, well… doesn't; their "good-guy" arch-nemesis; and an organization of heroes that may be less heroic than it appears. The story starts as a whimsical, frivolous parody of traditional heroic notions of good and evil -- and, with a sleight of hand, goes on to rework them as something entirely nuanced and authentic. What you’ll get is an interesting romp that is equal parts witty humor, action-adventure, and pathos soaked drama. <br /><br />Nimona and Ballister Blackheart make a perfect team. She may seem childish and annoying at times, but Blackheart's personality balances her out. One is childish, and the other is a genius -- the classic comedy double act you'd expect. As the story progresses, the character caricatures become real people you’ll get invested in and care about. <br /><br />The art perfectly suited the tone of the story, and the rich and contrasting colors made the artwork stand out in the best ways. I would’ve preferred the lettering just a bit bigger most of the time, but it's otherwise readable and legible. There are some unanswered questions, but that's expected being a short graphic novel. I would definitely say I was left wanting more. <br /><br />If you're looking for a humorous adventure that gets surprisingly deep, don't miss out on “Nimona”. It’s just one of those books where you just can’t help but care about the bad guys... who end up being not so bad after all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1355636176394014542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2154587641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3224459297908173819"><i>
  <b>"You can't just go around murdering people. There are rules, Nimona!" </b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508131104i/24184192._SX540_.png' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>Nimona</i> was such a fluffy yet meaningful read. It proves as a light escape from reality and into the world of dragons, heroic laws, good villains, broken doors and mostly SHARKS!!! I loved the art-style and the use of so many literary devices within the words and graphics that allowed the story to fly off the pages and straight into my heart. <br/>___________<br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Story</u>
</b><br/>This was nowhere near what I expected it to be. I was so </span>
  <span id="freeText3224459297908173819" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"You can't just go around murdering people. There are rules, Nimona!" </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508131104i/24184192._SX540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>Nimona</i> was such a fluffy yet meaningful read. It proves as a light escape from reality and into the world of dragons, heroic laws, good villains, broken doors and mostly SHARKS!!! I loved the art-style and the use of so many literary devices within the words and graphics that allowed the story to fly off the pages and straight into my heart. <br>___________<br><br><b>
  <u>The Story</u>
</b><br>This was nowhere near what I expected it to be. I was so happily shocked with where the story went that I recommend everyone go in blind with this one. <i>Nimona </i> was originally a web-comic series, and the author/artist even put the development of the character and the art at the latter pages of the novel. It showed me how hard it is to put an effective graphic novel together. <br><br>And it was, effective, that is. Because <i>Nimona </i> is a different story for everyone, it acts as a shapeshifting device itself. Because the story can shape shift its meaning for different people. That's the great thing about comics or graphic novels. You aren't just working on words. You are working with elements of art too. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508131842i/24184231._SX540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><b>
  <u>Blackheart</u>
</b><br>This cinnamon roll needed a section to himself, because I have never seen a villain so pure and so hero-like. <br>The development of Ballister is one that you see right at the end. It's worth it. So so so worth it. <br>He's a very multi-dimensional character in the sense, even though he tends to say the least - the message screams out the most. <br><br>Can we also take a moment...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508131842i/24184230._SY540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>No comment.<br><br><br><b>I loved every swirly wirly red minute of this novel and this review is now a shark.</b></span>

    <a title="María" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17754092-mar-a"><img alt="María" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504270585p2/17754092.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1862088071?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="María" class="user" itemprop="url" name="María" href="/user/show/17754092-mar-a">María</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1862088071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2316870079695177044">Nimona es una jovencita cambiaformas que decide convertirse en la ayudante de un temible súpervillano -con un oscuro pasado, por cierto-. Hasta ahí, puede parecer simplón. Pero no os dejéis engañar por eso. Nimona es divertida, tierna, con humor. A medida que avanza la trama se va salpicando igualmente de momentos de oscuridad. Además, le da una patada a los estereotipos. Ay, en serio, no todas las mujeres tenemos cintura de avispa y pechos gigantescos. La protagonista es una chica bajita, con c</span>
  <span id="freeText2316870079695177044" style="display:none">Nimona es una jovencita cambiaformas que decide convertirse en la ayudante de un temible súpervillano -con un oscuro pasado, por cierto-. Hasta ahí, puede parecer simplón. Pero no os dejéis engañar por eso. Nimona es divertida, tierna, con humor. A medida que avanza la trama se va salpicando igualmente de momentos de oscuridad. Además, le da una patada a los estereotipos. Ay, en serio, no todas las mujeres tenemos cintura de avispa y pechos gigantescos. La protagonista es una chica bajita, con caderas y muslotes, y no olvidéis que su corte de pelo es dios. La cosa no acaba ahí, el malo (que no es tan malo, ni los buenos tan buenos) tiene un brazo robótico. Y encima, el romantiqueo de la historia no recae sobre los personajes femeninos. En cuanto a dibujo y color: orgasmo visual.<br /><br />Nimona es una mezcla perfecta de fantasía medieval, ciencia ficción y muchos, muchos tiburones. Dedicado a todas esas "monster-girls". <br /><br />P.D: Que alguien me traiga una pizza a domicilio.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288179284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13528850529747023972"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433639528i/15124882.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I couldn't put this down. Besides the art being gorgeous and the colors being mesmerizing, the story itself was so compelling. It's an instant recommendation for anyone who enjoys graphic novels. <br/><br/>Ballister Blackheart is a super villain and Nimona is a shapshifter who wants to be his evil sidekick. Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin (yes, the name is great) is the hero, works for the law enforcement of this story, and is Ballister's arch-enemy! These three characters weave this amazing tale that makes the </span>
  <span id="freeText13528850529747023972" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433639528i/15124882.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I couldn't put this down. Besides the art being gorgeous and the colors being mesmerizing, the story itself was so compelling. It's an instant recommendation for anyone who enjoys graphic novels. <br><br>Ballister Blackheart is a super villain and Nimona is a shapshifter who wants to be his evil sidekick. Sir Ambrosius Goldenloin (yes, the name is great) is the hero, works for the law enforcement of this story, and is Ballister's arch-enemy! These three characters weave this amazing tale that makes the reader question three things:<br><br>1.)Is the hero really a good person? <br>2.)Is the villain really a bad person?<br>3.)Can one person be both?<br><br>Can <i>we</i> be both? People can be selfish and do horrible things. People can make mistakes, but can also be redeemed by their actions. I think the whole message make the world a little brighter, or hell, at least a little more tolerable. <br><br>I found this amazing web-comic a while back, and it totally blew me away. When I found out it was being published as a graphic novel, I knew I had to buy it and review it so I could sing it's praises (since I refuse to review 20 page comics, volume after volume, on Goodreads). <br><br>I am also in love with Noelle Sevenson's work with the amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300876456" rel="nofollow noopener">Lumberjanes</a> comics. I recommend both of these pieces of art. They are filled with humor, acceptance and love. These are both graphic novel gems! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433451715i/15098748._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Did I mention how gorgeous this book cover and every page inside it is? <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>

<div id="review_1283034987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283034987" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283034987?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062278227" href="/book/show/23131087-nimona">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283034987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4623671040859450175">This was very good but it made me sad. :( So I can't give it five stars. I was too sad.<br/><br/>Lord Blackheart is a "villain." But actually not. He's a good guy who never wants anyone to die and is actually only fighting against the evil Institution which rules this land. He acts like an old grumpy man and is obsessed with science. <br/><br/>One day an energetic young woman (15? ish?) shows up. She is a very powerful shapeshifter and she wants to help Blackheart take down the Institution.<br/><br/>...<br/><br/>THE GOOD:<br/><br/> - Nimona is </span>
  <span id="freeText4623671040859450175" style="display:none">This was very good but it made me sad. :( So I can't give it five stars. I was too sad.<br /><br />Lord Blackheart is a "villain." But actually not. He's a good guy who never wants anyone to die and is actually only fighting against the evil Institution which rules this land. He acts like an old grumpy man and is obsessed with science. <br /><br />One day an energetic young woman (15? ish?) shows up. She is a very powerful shapeshifter and she wants to help Blackheart take down the Institution.<br /><br />...<br /><br />THE GOOD:<br /><br /> - Nimona is chubby. And she's a shapeshifter and could choose to look like ANYONE but still chooses to be her chubby little redhead self. That is such a powerful message for readers.<br /><br /> - Nimona is a high-energy, bloodthirsty, murdurous young female - but also cute and at times vulnerable. Very exciting.<br /><br /> - Nimona's personality sparks brilliantly with Blackheart's more staid, cautious, moral, and science-obsessed one. Very cute.<br /><br /> - Gay characters and homosexual love as a great and completely normal thing - this is an actual baseline of the novel, NOT a sideplot.<br /><br /> - Great dialogue, story, and character development.<br /><br />THE BAD:<br /><br /> - The art. I just don't like it very much.<br /><br /> - It's sad.<br /><br /> - I was very upset and frustrated with Blackheart - not only with his morality and determination not to kill anyone (I know, I'm a monster) - but at times during the novel he just completely suffers from what seems to be a lobotomy. Just becomes basically an idiot in order to push the plot forward. This happens with no particular rhyme or reason and it annoyed me greatly.<br />...<br /><br />Tl;dr - I can't give this five stars, because it made me sad.<br /><br />You might mock me for that, but there you go.<br /><br />Great trinity of feminist comics I would check out if I were you:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22554204.Lumberjanes__Vol__1_Beware_the_Kitten_Holy" title="Lumberjanes, Vol. 1 Beware the Kitten Holy by Noelle Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Lumberjanes, Vol. 1</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20299683.Rat_Queens__Vol__1_Sass___Sorcery" title="Rat Queens, Vol. 1 Sass &amp; Sorcery by Kurtis J. Wiebe" rel="nofollow noopener">Rat Queens, Vol. 1: Sass &amp; Sorcery</a><br />and this, Nimona.<br /><br />Feminism is really exploding in the graphic-novel world right now. :D<br /><br />P.S. Not available in Spanish. French? Yes. Spanish? No. Come on, people. You're pissing me off.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4623671040859450175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1334722063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1334722063" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1334722063?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38898402-nimona">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334722063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6434458371797244840"><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 Stars</b> <br/><br/>So this is definitely one of the <u>cutest</u> graphic novels I've read in 2017.<br/><br/>I first want to highlight how great of a character Nimona is. I mean, just look at her. She's a big girl. Shaved head. Piercings. Oh, and she's a <b>fucking shapeshifter.</b> <br/><br/>She's a badass with an attitude & an unshakable desire to be an evil sidekick. I mean, I'm not sure what else you could want in a main character? <br/><br/>Anyway, Nimona herself is definitely one of the high points in this comic & I love how h</span>
  <span id="freeText6434458371797244840" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 Stars</b> <br /><br />So this is definitely one of the <u>cutest</u> graphic novels I've read in 2017.<br /><br />I first want to highlight how great of a character Nimona is. I mean, just look at her. She's a big girl. Shaved head. Piercings. Oh, and she's a <b>fucking shapeshifter.</b> <br /><br />She's a badass with an attitude &amp; an unshakable desire to be an evil sidekick. I mean, I'm not sure what else you could want in a main character? <br /><br />Anyway, Nimona herself is definitely one of the high points in this comic &amp; I love how her relationship develops with Ballister Blackheart, aka local, reluctant evil villain. It gave me warm feelings to see them interact &amp; watch them learn lessons in friendship from each other. <br /><br />To add to it, this graphic novel also has a great supporting cast. Blackheart, Goldenloin, and the Director, to be specific. <b>It's safe to say we've got an A+ in the character department.</b><br /><br />Another plus (or two) is the art style &amp; the humor. The combination of these two things really put me in mind of Adventure Time. It's witty without being overpowering &amp; lines up well with tone set by the illustrations. <br /><br /><b>Especially during action scenes, I love Stevenson's use of onomatopoeia &amp; color scheme.</b> <br /><br />Now we come to the parts I didn't love quite as much. <br /><br />For one, I really would've liked a bit more detail/depth added to the dynamic between Blackheart &amp; Goldenloin. The nature of their relationship is heavily implied, <b>but it's never outright confirmed</b> &amp; I think I would've gone with less subtlety, personally. <br /><br />I'm also a bit fuzzy on what actually <i>happened</i> at the end of this story. Like, I'm not sure I understand how things turned out the way they did. Either way, the ending was more abrupt that I would've liked &amp; because of that I feel like it didn't fully address all the questions the narrative brought to the surface. <br /><br /><b>All in all, a very enjoyable &amp; quick read.</b> This is the direction I want more comics &amp; graphic novels to take. I would've liked just a bit more from this, but I really enjoyed my time with these characters &amp; I'm glad I can finally stick this on my 'Read' shelf!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6434458371797244840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1426334505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426334505" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1343990885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343990885" />
    <a title="♛Tash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5451856-tash"><img alt="♛Tash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456286012p2/5451856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1343990885?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♛Tash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♛Tash" href="/user/show/5451856-tash">♛Tash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062278227" href="/book/show/23131087-nimona">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1343990885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9364831719729129966"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453759702i/17869003.jpg' alt='Nimona sticker!: ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>At first shift, Nimona is the story of a skilled, yet impulsive, villain side kick and her ornery master, Ballister Blackheart. I was expecting the classic mentor-mentee relationship ala Batman and Robin, but I was pleasantly surprised that it's way more than that. Let's just say it's more like Batman and Joker.Together, they do whatever it is villainous duos do, create chaos and mayhem, and work on fulfilling personal vendettas against the Institution and their #1 hero Sir Goldenlion.<br/><br/>Though I a</span>
  <span id="freeText9364831719729129966" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453759702i/17869003.jpg" alt="Nimona sticker!: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At first shift, Nimona is the story of a skilled, yet impulsive, villain side kick and her ornery master, Ballister Blackheart. I was expecting the classic mentor-mentee relationship ala Batman and Robin, but I was pleasantly surprised that it's way more than that. Let's just say it's more like Batman and Joker.Together, they do whatever it is villainous duos do, create chaos and mayhem, and work on fulfilling personal vendettas against the Institution and their #1 hero Sir Goldenlion.<br><br>Though I am not that accustomed to reading graphic novels anymore, I found Nimona to be such a fun read I would no doubt revisit often for a quick laugh. I personally loved Ballister Blackheart's character, he's complex, has a deadpan humor and a big heart.Yes, a villain with a big heart. In a kingdom so hung up on labels, Blackheart was more of a nuisance than a real threat because of his reticence to kill, until Nimona comes along. Their relationship develop from wary tolerance to guarded acceptance and eventually genuine friendship. The development was adorably well done.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453759427i/17868985._SY540_.jpg" alt="Nimona chapter 5 - page 17 | Gingerhaze Seriously is us watching movies: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The story takes a darker turn as Blackheart and Nimona graduate from petty acts of villainy to full blown atrocities. They discover Institution secrets that'll further blur the line between heroism and villainy. The turns of the story are somewhat predictable, but that's not necessarily a bad thing given that it was fast-paced and reinforced with a witty dialogue.<br><br><b>But why the 3.5 stars?</b> I am not that fond of the artwork. This is irrelevant to the story itself, but I like to have a solid picture of the main characters. Until now, I am uncertain whether she's wearing a pink skull cap or she has a buzzcut with bangs. Better detailed backgrounds and more facial expressions would have been wonderful too. That being said,for the kind of storyline Nimona has, a graphic novel is the most effective format.<br><br>Overall, Nimona is a wonderful character and dialogue driven graphic novel I would recommend to people who are interested to explore the genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9364831719729129966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1U9BfcZ6RhByPd3xq5qCvjI1cVIizTKh29rjYv/Wvq1A02tzJx9gcuKJmQWN9ME6J8/pJsITc+MrY00Ybn++Zw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+JLDsSPTu6bMILILucoSFNnr78JnxeVGBP3m/9QNCxptDum/wradxFyU9v+fpFGQzBF3tocbpAT0REiFRaQL0A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6887314.Noelle_Stevenson">About Noelle Stevenson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17053919899814284668">Noelle Stevenson is a comic artist and freelance illustrator residing in Los Angeles, California. She published the young adult graphic novel NIMONA in 2015, which is also serialized online . She has been nominated for a Harvey Award, and was awarded the Slate Cartoonist Studio Prize for Best Webcomic in 2012. She is a graduate of the Maryland Institute College of Art and has done published work f</span>
  <span id="freeText17053919899814284668" style="display:none">Noelle Stevenson is a comic artist and freelance illustrator residing in Los Angeles, California. She published the young adult graphic novel NIMONA in 2015, which is also serialized online . She has been nominated for a Harvey Award, and was awarded the Slate Cartoonist Studio Prize for Best Webcomic in 2012. She is a graduate of the Maryland Institute College of Art and has done published work for BOOM! Studios, Random House, MacMillan Press, and What Pumpkin Studios, among others. She is the co-writer of LUMBERJANES, a comic series from BOOM! Box, and has done writing work for Frederator's BRAVEST WARRIORS as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17053919899814284668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
